So, fun fact about Shuckle - it was actually based on snake wine, which is wine fermented with a snake in it (a traditional practice from China).  The beta design of Shuckle is simply a snake head poking out of a jar, its "legs" were much smaller and looked like part of the "jar".  For whatever reason, this design, like many others in Gen 2, was toned down to make it a vaguely turtle-like creature, but the stuff about it fermenting fruit in its shell remained.

Pumpkaboo and its evolution likely aren't edible pumpkins. There's multiple different types, bred specifically for one purpose or the other. The pumpkins bred for carving, like the pumpkins these PokÃ©mon inhabit, are not bred to be consumed, and thus don't have a pleasant taste and are a bit dry. Pie pumpkins, on the other hand, have thicker guts and a better taste. That's just my understanding, at least

Weird fun food facts that nobody asked for.  Garlic is a natural bug repellent (primarily with mosquitos) when ingested, similar to the dex entry for petlil. Pumpkin flavored dishes such as pumpkin pie don't actually have pumpkin in them. It's actually butternut squash that is used as the USDA allows anything in the gourd group to be labeled as pumpkin for some reason. Actual pumpkin is actually fairly bitter and unappetizing to most Americans, so the much sweeter butternut squash is used instead. Also, pumpkin spice is just the spices that would be added to the "pumpkin" when making pumpkin pie. There is no actual pumpkin (or squash) used in anything labeled as pumpkin spice.

For those who don't know, Farfetch'd's Japanese name is a phrase which translates to "a duck comes bearing green onions," which is a Japanese figure of speech meaning "surprising, but convenient."  So its entire original premise was that it's a joke about a duck that carries its own side vegetable.

Not that I'd volunteer myself to eat any bug-type pokemon, but there are a lot of edible bugs irl. I've heard that Spiders and Scorpions taste like Crab, while things like ants, crickets, and mealworms generally have earthy/nutty flavors. And since bugs are often pretty low on the food chain, they tend to be very abundant and replenish their populations very efficiently.  So we could probably build out a pretty large list of potentially edible bug-type pokemon, avoiding anything potentially toxic (poison type), or overly dangerous (who's gonna put their neck on the line to taste what a Scizor's claw meat tastes like?).  Caterpie, Wurmple, Kricketot, Grubbin, Blipbug, Surskit, Yanmega, Dwebble, Wimpod, Dewpider, and Araquanid would be by picks for potentially edible bug-types. They're on the small side, but what bugs lack in size, they unfortunately make up for in sheer quantity,

Okay. I don't like having to remind people of this, but whatever. The pumpkin flavour is different from pumpkin spice. Pumpkins themselves don't taste that special, it's only when you add the pumpkin seasonings that make it taste good. Pumpkin spice is a mix of cinnamon, nutmeg, and ginger, along with various other spices, but those are the main ones. So a "pumpkin spice flavoured anything" doesn't have pumpkin in it. It has cinnamon, nutmeg, and ginger. Not pumpkin.  Baby power, on the other hand, definitely has babies in it.
